自由談

奈何

— 非心

相傳有過這樣的笑話：王荆公常不洗頭面，面目　黑，非常難看，侍者進澡豆，請他洗臉，荆公説：『天生黑於予，澡豆其如予何』！『其如予何』，翻成白話，便是『將奈我何』！或『將把我怎樣』！孔夫子説過『桓　其如予何』！王莽也説過『漢兵其如予何』！皆是到了沒有辦法的地步，這麽説的　。

如果要在『幽默』項下舉例，這倒是極好的例子。

不過這種氣分，在近代也不多見了，一味崛强，貫澈到底，也略有外强中乾的意味，矯情鎭物的嫌疑。這種話説出了當然使人覺得可笑，然雖到了這種地步而不説出，那情况是多的。

這妙法一經傳佈開去，實行起來，天下就要不平安了。當然，聰明人只當他『幽默』，一笑而已；傻子就會認眞，處處崛强起來，『其如予何』呢？許多地方要使人弄到沒有辦法的。那精義，就是無所畏了。最高的限度不過一死，死後怎樣無從知道，姑不必論，但每人只有一生死，却是的確的。世間事無論眞幻，最

大無過於生死之情。如果有所畏，畏到極致也無非怕死而已。然而孔夫子早不怕死了，王莽也不怕，王安石更不怕，好像説：我生來是這麽一個人，你們這班東西將奈我何呢？所以王安石説：天變不足畏，人言不足恤，祖宗不足法！

時下無論『站在那種立塲』看，中國的確近於危亡，然就正需要一班不怕人，不怕鬼，不怕三敎九流，高文典册，金科玉律，炸彈手槍······的人，擴充仁道的精神，動手救這危亡的民族！

當然，也還得不怕『澡豆』！

自己介紹

— 汗靑

近來社會上有一種很時髦的風氣，特别流行於士大夫階級間。這風氣還沒有適當的名稱，姑名之爲『自己介紹』。

翻開報紙來看，我們時常會看到『介紹』的一欄。大抵介紹人多半是社會上知名之士、而被介紹的人十九都是什麽『懷才不遇』，『曲高和寡』的人物。在現代組織複雜的社會裏，人和人的關係斷不像從前閉關時代那麽簡單。『介紹人才』的需要，當不在『介紹書籍』；『介紹東西』的需要下。不過介紹人當老老實實地把被介紹的人的履歷和本領很扼要地叙述出來，不要把陳篇累牘的套語都加在被介紹的人的身上、免得讀者誤會爲他是在看廣告，反將『介紹』的原意失掉了。可是介紹的文字如寫得過火，讀者還可以原諒他的苦衷。因爲我們貴國的同胞最講究體面，寗可虚張誇大，斷不可樸實精當。這就是説，一個人的本領只有五分，你最少也要把他吹嘘到十分。不然，被介紹的人不但不給你道謝，而且會結成無謂的寃家。因此，介紹的文字寫得越漂亮，而讀者的心裏也越給牠打個很大的折扣。

介紹人的文字旣失掉作用，於是一般狡滑者流，又發明一種『自已介紹』的方法。

如説，現在外國有一個大學敎授或作家逝世，他的友生和愛好的讀者，要寫些詩文在報紙雜誌上追悼，本是人『情』正當的表示，毫無非議的地方。可是有一種人在追悼老師的文章裏，要硬派他的老師是當代無雙的聖人，學行兼優，弟子遍天下，簡直是孔子蘇格拉底再生。接着便把死者的學生的姓名按照交遊的先後寫出來

，並自謂本人是死者最得意的高足，彷彿要把自己的地位與顏子和柏拉圖同列。臨了，還在報紙的下面登了一條本人著作集的詳細廣告，聊表『學有淵源』。吁，巧矣哉，『自己介紹』的心理也！

其實，『自己介紹』並不是一件壞事，只要自己拿出眞正本事給人看，人家自然會佩服，用不着徒費唇舌來自吹自擂。我們看毛遂自薦的故事時，心

情只有同情贊羡，覺得他的行動不愧爲英雄本色。他不虚張他的家世是怎樣高明，他不援引他的老師是怎樣聖哲，他不誇耀自己在家族和師友的關係中是佔什麽地位，他只要找個適當的機會來表演自己的本領罷了。

『桃李不言，下自成蹊』。我希望國内的靑年志士努力養成學行兼優的完人，不要妄自菲薄，致陷於『因人成事』的地步。眞正的本領，終久總有人賞識，何必採取這種表彰死人，其實是蓄意提拔自己的妙計呢。

二十二年十二月二十六日於北平

吊肉香

— 炎辛

幾個壯漢在菩薩面前，磕了頭，許下心願。

平常荒凉得　現的關武廟裏，這時却熱烘烘地，

男女老壯都到，嚷着，閙着。

壯漢們捋出鐵般地臂膊，站穩了脚，兩兩碰着。初兒輕輕地，隨後愈撞愈凶。咬緊下唇，顯然在拼

命了，全堂就哄笑起來。『嚇！别高興，時辰一到怕就會軟下來咧！』

癩痢頭擠眉弄眼，滑出了嘴。壯漢們還沒伸出拳兒，癩痢已從人叢混走

。

時辰終於到了。壯漢們走進神龕背面去了。大家還是站在堂前，嚷着，閙着。

『他們無非想吃一頓夜飯吧？』

『有錢進腰包啦！』

『呸！是報答娘恩啦！』

種種論調貼在每一個人的口頭。但是，『報娘恩』

的觀念，隱在每人的心裏。據説吊過肉香，娘的養育深恩就算報答了。

『看啦！看啦！出來了啦！』

遠站着的反先喊出了口，打野眼的人，也注視着了。

鐵般地左臂膀密排着鈎，鈎下繫着細線，細線歸綜到一支粗繩，粗繩下面，繫着大銅鑼。足足地把皮吊下三寸。還有繫着笨重地香爐的，連皮帶肉垂了下來。

『阿彌陀佛』，『行手千眼』。老婆婆呶着嘴，唸起佛來了。

壯漢們嚴肅地站在菩薩面前。前三進，後三退。蕩着香爐，打着大鑼。他們凖備出發了。大家爭扎地湧出廟門。嚷着，閙着。鑼聲人聲混在一堆。

壯漢在街市遊行啦！他們碰到道塲人家，就在門前做『三進三退』的儀節。道塲人家設着齋臺，臺上供着偶像。什麽關公啦！岳爺啦！五虎將啦！

ＸＸＸ

這吊肉香，果眞是報娘的恩麽？不，不。依據一種傳説，這算是民族思想的表現哩！傳説是這樣的：『明朝崇禎皇帝吊殺煤山後，漢人就做了滿淸的奴隸。他們屈服在統治者威權之下，祇得飲氣呑聲；有牢騷，祗得借題發揮。這『報娘恩』，就是他們做出忍痛的樣態，表示不甘屈服的英勇的。因此

，他們舉行的時期，是每年三月崇禎吊殺的月份。他們所崇拜的，都是關，

岳。五虎將。等民族英雄一。

這種深入民間的民族運動，在今日，是被取締的了。現在所有的，是智識階級的民族文學，和學生們口中的『抵抗』了！

吃飯的文章

— 繩夫

素來看不起文人的湘溪據説現在他自己也成爲文人了。不過，一直到現在止，我却未曾拜讀過他的作品。這大槪是因爲我不知道他用的是什麽筆名的緣故罷。我祗聽得冬生説，他現在不開礦了，因爲生活難過，也祗得替幾家刋物寫些文章，藉以　養活他的妻及三個孩子。但是，這話我早在半年前就聽進耳了，我們終究無緣一晤。

我心中常常想到，他大槪在撰述些關於科學的文字罷。我在有意無意間，也常注意雜誌　紙上的關於科學的文字。不過，這類文字是不能辦别一個人的個性的，因此也就不能斷定，這些文字中那一篇是出於湘溪的手筆。

近月來我又聽到朋友説，湘溪也就同住在西市了。幾次想去一訪，却因相别過久了，不知道這位故人還能相識不？他不是很潦倒麽？他是否有心緒來叙舊呢？這些念頭每次又將我去訪問的心情打碎了。

後來我從冬生口中得到湘溪最近生活狀况，却並不像我想像的壞，據説，他也尙未將我遺忘，也有相晤一談的心願，不過也因爲相别太久，不好造次來的訪似的。

於是，我同冬生先去訪問他。

大槪是因爲我們都是『曾經滄海』的人了罷。相見也是很平淡的。大家叙了一回寒暄，也就找不到其他的話可説了。在這相對默然的時候，我却發現了他的書案上的一束原稿，我於是走近案頭，急欲一翻故人所從事的『勝業』時，他却現出很難爲情的樣子，冷冷的笑道：

『無聊得很，吃飯的文章。』

『你不用客氣。聽説你久改行了。你年來的著作一定很有可觀罷！』

『著作？』他有點惱了，順手將那一束原稿向我一擲，繼續道：『你看了這篇東西，就知道我的一切了。

我忙將原稿紙拉伸，在第一行上看見他用大號字題上：

『元旦試筆』四字·我幾乎爲之茫然，因爲現在隔新年足足還有二十多天，爲何急性乃爾，竟將『元旦試筆』提前寫出？

『你覺得我太無聊了罷！』

他苦笑了。『這是替ＸＸ市』

家雜誌寫的。他們元旦要印出，約我在付印前一星期寄一到，我不得不提前來寫。本來寫這類文字無聊己極，二十年前做孩子的時候，在父親的監督下，是年年要寫一次的。不過，當時確是應景，另有一番愉快的心情，比起現在拏這類文字來賣錢，眞是不可同日而語罷：其實，這也是非意料所及的。』他有點慨然了。

我還有什麽話可說呢。他的『勝業』確在這篇文字中得到說明。我並未將這篇文字唸完。我已看出他心頭是在如何的妻絶，悲冷和憤懣。我將這束文稿裝上封袋裏了，我們都不禁爲之默然。

同時我感着慚愧了。我後悔我們相見時那一套客氣的寒暄，竟有點帶着嘲笑的氣分。我不知故人能諒我不？現在我們又有數十天不相見了。我一想到今年出版界的蕭條，寫文章的題材和地盤也日狹一日，我不能不爲這位孤高的有三個孩子的父母親擔心。不知『吃飯的文章』是否能飽他家五六人的飢腹呢？

鄉村之夜

— 毅弘

聽遠處傳來的寺鐘幽玄，舒緩地，

滑過這凝寂的寒江；

寒江底翠波涒鄰地奏着琤琮的音。看西天塗抺着的一片酡紅的光霞，呈着如火災時的回映，顯然地，

畫出了都市底煥煌。

像猙獰的怔忡在陰黝中的魅魑啊！

－－是一族的松子。

幾陣凉爽的微風，

淅淅地，把牠的影子吹亂了，

溜出來陣陣凄惋的　　聲。

深巷的餓犬嘹喨地一聲，

劃破了靜謐的四野；

原來是

竹林深處，緩緩地移動着數盞燈火。

如水樣純潔的大氣中，

時間着數聲村墟的夜春。素淡的月華沐着疎落的茅舍；

疏林裏隱現着幾粒的燈火；

冷冰的四野，織聲和着蟲聲。沉醉在都市裏的人們喲！

可能意想到人間有如許的幽境。只等那晨鷄動野，荷鋤的田父踽踽地彳亍在田塍上的時分，都市的人們喲！許是爲了整夜的勞瘁。正尋打着酣睡中的夢味。

五·十·於杭州

歐靜麗Ｅｕｇｅｎｉｅ（四）

— 白韋

兩方面整個拒絶，並不使玄灰心，他早已發誓要排除一切困難、終生保有歐靜麗！不過歐靜麗方面却不同了，她是十足地具有女性的實際主義的！她不願過分違背她母親的意思，她雖是不信宗敎的，却不願一個宗敎的處罰，使她家庭在鄰里前，减少風光。她知道一般世俗的人們，是沒有方法可以使他們了解她自身的情形的。玄勸她索性抛棄了家庭，她不肯接受這個意思，她主張緩進政策：他和她還年靑；她要得到母親的同意，敎長的特許以　後，才和玄訂婚。玄的雄辯不能改變這女孩的固執！於是婚約的一回事，便暫時停頓下來。目前，無論如何，他倆總是享受着人世間可能的美滿的生活！他倆又第二回同度過了冬季和春天，歐靜麗還是那樣嬌美溫婉，和玄第一天會見她的時候一樣！

第二學年的考試又快要到來。這是歐靜麗大學本科最後兩張文憑的考試。玄一想到這可咀咒的暑假，不容情地迫近了，又得把他的歐靜麗送去，他惶急起來。

『歐靜麗，下學年你還來讀研究院嗎？』他倆同侍在小花園裏的木凳上，濃綠的榆葉　覆着他倆。

『不一定。我最初只和家庭約定，兩年讀完四張文憑的，並不曾談到取得學士學位以　後。再讀研究院，因爲那時根本不能料到兩年究竟能否考過四張文憑不能呢。我這回到家。自然和家庭商量，再來讀研究院。親愛的，我如何能長久地　開你！我想，我還要返巴黎的！』

『假若你家庭爲離隔我倆起見，竟不許你再來呢？』玄懷疑地問。

『便是這婚事，我也預備回家進行去。』她很有把握似地説。

『進行不成功呢？』

歐靜麗沒有立刻回答。玄舉起她的右手，送到嘴邊去舐吻，眼涙滴在她掌上。『那也不要緊！我一達到法律上的成年，我便可以自由地到巴黎來，我的父母不復能拘管我。我便同你到中國去。好不好？』歐靜麗安慰玄，抱攏他的頭，在他額上親吻。

『那時候我倆就結婚了？』

『那又不同。那時候我雖然可以自由和你同來同去，却只是我』個人的遊歷一樣。結婚却不行的！你想：我一和你結婚，牧師又和我家庭不干休了。我父親倒無所謂，我母親一定忍受不下鄰里的　笑的。你不知道我母親對於鄰里是如何保持着種尊嚴呢。

『照你説，我倆將來可以同居，而沒有方法結婚，就像現在一樣。』

『結婚的方法是有的：或者得到敎長的特許；或者我母親死去。』

『多麽矛盾的社會啊！』玄嘆息了。

歐靜麗忙着考試的時候，這問題沒有再被提起。勝利地通過考試以　後，她在巴黎休息了幾天，便和玄去遊歷柏林。她預備從那裏到維也納，趁船回國。

Page 21

談言『婦女國貨年』果失敗了嗎？

— 夢若

不必勞日文報來冷嘲熱諷，我們也早就知道所謂『婦女國貨年』是和『打倒帝國主義』一樣，不過是一種喊喊好聽，助助熱鬧的空口號而已，豈眞便能挽救這垂危的中國。中國摩登婦女之擯棄國貨，崇尙外貨，本是毫不足怪的，因其旣爲摩登，自然惟摩登的物品最能稱心合意。誰知一般多事的熱心提倡國貨者，偏要舉行這麽一個『婦女國貨年，』來苦勸她們服用國貨，且利用一個『愛國』的名義，冀能以打動她們的良心。結果不惟於事無補，反而落得給敵人嘲笑我們説：『國民政府盡其能力，利用所有宣傳機關，提倡國貨，特所謂婦女國貨年之口號，其期望成績，全歸泡影，何則，溯自正月以來，迄今己届四月有半，而本年度第一季之輸入超過額，爲一億六千萬元，按照數字而言，内中情形，一見可知，卽輸入之舶來品，大部分多在都市中消費，其間十之五六，全爲摩登婦女階級之裝飾消耗品，因此雖以提倡國貨之口號相號召，但婦女們的心中，則依然不問不聞，莫怪婦女國貨年之全歸失敗耳。

『婦女國貨年』的失敗，其原因的確在於『婦女的心中，則依然不問不聞，』

然而我們要提倡國貨，並不以婦女爲限，更並不以摩登婦女爲限，我們的目的，是在期望全國四萬萬同胞，能够一心一意，個個起來實行。我們之所以定訂今年爲『婦女國貨年』，只不過是想給婦女界以一個刺激，呌她們覺醒，其實也沒有多大用意。而且我們敢相信，我國提倡國貨的口號，雖然收效甚鮮，説半點影響也沒有，則又未必，我們只要看看近來上海一埠幾家國貨工廠和國貨商塲的勃興氣象，便可推想得到。所以我們以爲嘲諷儘管他們去嘲諷，提倡還是盡我們自己的力量來提倡。用一分努力，卽可收一分成績。本此信念，我們甚願熱心國貨運動的人士，繼續奮鬥下去，以達到我們最後的目的。

不過我們要提倡國貨，應脚踏實地苦幹下去，才得有效果，非弄什麽新花樣所能爲功。我們最宜注意的，是在國貨的改良和發明。改良可以使國貨由劣變優，和舶來品比美，發明可以製造出新貨物，和舶來品競爭，如此，國貨卽不提倡，國人也無有不樂用的。我們幾曾聽到英法德或日等國在提倡國貨，然而英美法總或日的人民、大都是喜用其本國的國貨的。可知國貨不在提倡，而在有優良的國貨給人民享用。

最後我們還得在這里來向中國一班摩登婦女進一言，中國如再不思振作，亡國是必然的結果，亡國的慘禍，不久便會在我們的眼前實現出來。怎樣振作，這端賴全國人民的覺醒，共赴危難，以挽回頽局。用服國貨，本是國人應有的本分。你們果尙存有一點愛國心，請從此起，來替國家盡一分義務。你們試想一想，敵人一面用經濟侵略的手段來亡我國，一面又在那里大放冷語，笑我國人沒有愛國心，對於這，你們覺得怎樣呢？眞敎我們痛心呵！

中國婦女的前途

— 波兒

我覺得，婦女問題是中國社會最大問題之一。站在人口的統計方面來説，我們不是有四萬萬同胞嗎？可是，在性的類别上，那末婦女是佔着半數了。但，連年的内戰，在砲火的陣綫上，中國不是犧牲了許多許多的男性嗎？在生理方面，我們再來考察一下，女性是多半弱於男性的，因爲在因　的重男輕女的社會裏，一切的問題，都以男性爲中心。所以，婦女方面漸漸地失了她們本能了，她們只幹些家庭内的細微的瑣碎的工作，結果，在康健上她們是比男性爲優的至少，她們是不必像男子那麽苦勞，她們沒有擔憂生活上的重大的責任，她們沒有受過像男子那般極度的操勞。所以，中國的婦女底壽命，往往是比男子長呢。由這種的情態來推測，中國的婦女是多於男子的，我以爲不會有錯誤罷。

基於這點的論斷，那末，佔着中國社會大半人口的婦女，顯明是一件十分重大的問題了。

可是，在這個畸形的社會制度下，女子是被蔑視的，被壓迫的，被剝削的，被排擠的，被禁錮於黑暗的地層的深處。

因此，婦女的悲劇日益加深了，在這無涯的痛苦底生活裏頭，女子不是受過了幾千年來的非人生活嗎？

在詩經『斯千』一首詩裏，我們來舉個例證罷：『乃生男子，載寢之牀······，家室君五···乃生女子，載寢之地，無非無儀，唯酒食是議，無父母詒罹···』

這分明，把女子當草艾，丢棄於地，總之女子是被擯棄，被蹂躪的了。然而，另一方面來説，一般太太小姐門的豐衣足食，過其浪漫豪闊的生活，這只是一種甘自墮落的現象，我們不能説她們是如何如何悲慘？

所以，我的論點是以廣大的勞苦婦女大衆爲中心。她們的生活是人間料想不到的黑暗，她們是受封建勢力的殘踏，有男性的虐待，在這些的重重壓制底下，中國婦女的前途，是會形成怎樣一個結果呢？向死裏日益埋沒了她們的生命！

所以，爲了毁滅這種不幸的悲劇，爲了爭得『男女平等』，爲了解放和自由，爲了權利，爲生存······那末，婦女必須要爭鬥起來，我們應該自信自己是『人』，並不是奴隸，並不是生來爲男子的所有品，更不是他們的玩具呢！

在思想方面，我們要努力洗脱了那些惡劣的殘舊觀念，養成一種科學的新時代的意識。在實際的實踐方面，我們要加倍的學習和爭取政治上經濟上敎育上枝術的……種種權益。這樣，我們才能走向光明的前途啊！

五月底風

— 蕙人

天色己夜了，沒有月亮，沒有星點，

黃浦江裏吹來的風啊，怪軟地沒有刺激，沒有芬芳。慘淡的電燈光照出了每一物件的輪廓，影子是瘦長的。江水無力的在擊拍着，音調是異常的沈悶。心田憂鬱地，像夜色一樣；望着朦朧的輪船，在想着故鄉啊！那裏有着甜甜的櫻桃，顏色是紅得可愛；還有那帶一點苦味的海水啊，曾洗着我底身體；

還有着堅强的眼珠，堅强的肐膊；還有那五月的風勢是猛烈的，空氣帶有着一點淸香；還有，那·········我相着啊，像在夢裏。

印在腦海裏的瑛姑娘。

白菓樹已經綠綠地生滿着葉子，在溫暖的風吹下，發出一陣陣有規律的充滿着詩意的聲息。我平臥在樹底下麗着早晨的日光，聽着樹葉中間的鶯語，看着頭領浮雲的飛駛：我唱着啊，那沒有節奏的拍子，微笑常常掛在嘴邊，我幸福着啊，在大自然的懷抱裏！

從東面的竹林裏忽然有着一聲尖鋭的呌喊，我跑過去看着，看着有什麽事件發生。是一個美麗的姑娘　在地上，裙子已經撕破了，臉色是怪模樣的灰白

Page 22

，手背上有一絲絲的血在流着。我用着手帕替她把創口輕輕地紥住，把帶來的熱水袋灑了一杯開水給她喝；神志一點點的淸楚了，臉色慢慢的在轉紅，眼珠也在活動了。

『什麽事，姑娘』？我輕輕地問着。『···········』那蘋菓般的臉是現出一陣羞紅，低下了頭在按摩着那隻滿手汚泥的手腕。

『倒底什麽事啊，姑娘』？我顯示出一點不煩。

『從樹上跌下來』，用手指着那一顆樹。

『怎樣會爬到樹上去的呢』？

『我愛着那樹上的鳥窠，裏面有着卵子呢』！

『但怎跌下來的呢』？我感覺到一點興趣的問着。

『那樹椏子上有着，有着·····一條小靑蛇啊』！臉上還現出驚慌的神態。『哈······哈······有趣，你受傷了沒有』？我不禁的笑着。

她搖了搖頭，表示並沒有受痛，並低下了頭天眞的笑着。

那時起我便熟識了她，知道了她的名字呌做瑛，那美麗的名字啊，我輕輕地淰着。她有着堅强的眼珠，堅强的肐膊，那被海水和日光曬黑了的手臂，發出一層亮亮的光彩。我們時常在白菓樹底下咬着櫻子，談着遙遠的故事；她那頑皮的性子，使我常用樹枝打着她的手心，那時她會逃往竹林裏躱住笑着，我便追着。這樣我們天天把光陰化在天眞

的淘氣裏。

我把無形中各自戀着了，我有一天不看見那頑皮的笑臉時，我便會一天做不得事。我想對她説：『瑛，我愛你啊』

！我也想寫一封信給她，以表示我心中的燃燒，但我見了那隻活潑的笑臉啊，我便失去了勇氣，在心間我會感覺得到自慚。

但是無情的六月輕輕地悄悄地降到了人間，我要回南去了啊，回到這無情的上海。

『瑛，别了』！像有一團棉花塞住了我的心間一樣。

『不要忘記給我帶些南方的故事來啊』！眼珠仍是那麽地堅强，沒有留戀，沒有悲哀。

『好吧，你給我帶來故鄉的故事一樣』。

輪船一點點的離開了堅强的風土，望着那揮着手的影子一點點的淡下去。五月的風啊，已悄悄地又降到人間，我望着迷朧的輪船想信故鄉的風啊，那醉人的風，給我帶走吧，到那甜蜜的故鄉！

襲尹霞女士的死因（續）

— 魏慈

由此，我們可以説，龔女士的痛苦是社會給予的，龔女士的生命是自己斷送的，追究起來，這事件的本身責任，還是要由龔女士自己負擔。社會環境旣已不適合我們的生活要求了，我們就要拒絶牠，並改造牠，這就是革命的根源，社會進化的起點。譬如多數個人的貧窮，是社會釀成的，然而由貧窮迫成的盜竊行爲，却還是應由個人負責，這在現行社會制度裏固屬是犯罪的行爲卽依社會主義的理論來説，他們亦應大家一致起來積極的求有以改造社會，不應以消極的個人主義用盜竊手段解决一時的生活問題。

龔女士的自殺是錯了。我希望由龔女士的死，一方面使婦女界能起來舊事重提的再做一點提高婦女在社會心理中的地位的工夫，消潔大家庭組織的潛勢，肅淸封建思想所加於女性的遺毒。這話説來似太陳腐太平淡，若大家肯去新舊家庭中實際體察，便可知這勢力在社會在家庭中所加於女性的虐待之嚴重性了。在另一方面却希望凡受着外來刺激－－不論精神的物質的，使得心靈疲弱到無力自持惟想着自殺的人們，請趕快將你的頭腦冷靜下來，反省到自己其所以不堪壓迫和痛苦並找不着一條出路的原因，完全是因爲自己對事認識未淸，理解未透，才無力救助自己，才無勇氣提負自己的責任，並非社會上眞沒有你的出路，不信，請看龔尹霞就是一例－－她是自己阻塞了自己的出路。（完）

打拳的哲學

— 白榕

我們打人家一拳，往往可得到下列三種不同的結果：

（一）把那人打倒了。

（二）那人回敬一拳，把你打倒了。

（三）那人完全不　睬你。

第一種是足以證明你的力氣大，可以博得人們的讚譽與欽佩，第二種雖然失敗，可是至少還足以證明你有相當的力氣，你這一拳竟能刺激對方，引起反應，只有第三種，打上去的時候，不痛不癢，人家的淡漠正足以證明你的無力，可以説是失敗之尤，所以我們可以大膽地説上一句，打拳而得到第三種結果的　可以説是全無出息。

自己懂得打下去不會有結果、知難而退地畏縮起來，雖然如糊紙老虎一樣可憐，可是至少還可以在别人面前綳綳架子。打下去是會露出自己本相的，你不打，人家當然無從測知你的眞相是什麽樣子。在自己的眞相還沒給人家猜破的時候，暗暗地磨拳擦掌，靜候時機，一旦元氣旺盛，功夫純熟，掄手朝那人要害砸上一拳，卽使沒打倒地，至少要引起他喊兩聲『啊呀！』，或是轉身照樣回敬你一下，這樣，纔不失爲聰明的辦法。

從前有人説：『外交當有武力爲後盾』，又説：『弱國無外交』，在目前形勢上考查起來，這兩句話還是把捉住一部份的眞理的。最近日本人在天津八里台造飛機塲，我國又開始抗議了。在過去，抗議的把戲似乎與我們非常熟悉。大槪自從中日有了關係以來，我們就不斷地做着『抗議』的功夫，然而也只是抗議而已。緊張的面容和揮舞的手勢往往因了對方的淡漠而鬆弛下來。過去的歷史已經給我們以深刻的敎訓：爲什麽我們抗議人家不來答理？爲什麽别人的抗議就是那麽有力？這問題的焦點在怎麽地　？能够認淸這問題而　以解答，退一步培養自己潛力的，纔是一個弱者最適當的辦法。否則東抗一下。西抗一下，弄得人家毫無影響，而自己精力俱疲，氣血交虧，結果是可憐的束手待斃，那纔眞是不識時務的大傻瓜。

打拳不是容易的事。怎樣去打？怎麽時候去打？打誰？什麽地方是他的要害？都關係全局的勝負，揮舞拳頭的人，曾否對這加以一度冷靜深切的思慮呢？

弗如意傳（五）

— 忘我

無垠缺陷

— 列火

至少，在過去與現在理想與事實是嶄然的兩回事，絶不能印證和諧，而是相承相生，如影隨形的幻離着，始終成爲一個謎。

但，很有些説，理想是事實之母，是事實的先導，那是他們活把『人』與『環境』看作似一個雕刻的石像，是靜的，是死的，忽視了『動』中演進的意義，正如天象的風雨晦明，人間，魔術幻燈，一些兒都捉摸不住。

這輩人，爲着要證明他們的理論眞實可靠，慣把一些不甚落實的事情拿來做考證，力圓其説，有時候也彷彿説得很像，比如『民國』是辛亥革命以前的理想，辛亥以後，『民國』畢竟成了事實。太平天國肇事之始，不獨是滅淸復明『而且飽含有社會主義的思潮，如『打富濟民』等口號，可見一斑。就是分子之間，當時也是緊相策應，毫無介蒂，儼然可以完成理想似的。可是後來怎樣呢？到了江山垂成，奠都金陵時，理想就成了一縷暮烟似隱消了。誰都忘了他的使命，幾個首領，只顧利害的傾軋，明爭暗鬥，結果是自相殘殺，白送給曾左彭一個大獻身手的機會。所謂太平天國，就如一朶　花。盛衰之暫，每使後之作史者椎胸無語。

就説現今的事，『九一八』以來，『抗日救國』是一個理想，大槪誰都有這麽一個理想，只除了甘冒不韙的鄭老狗等以外，其餘如主張『五十年』『十年』後而談『救國』的洋聖人老博士，也都總有這麽一個理想。但事實却偏偏中途起了歪曲，陳擺在我們眼前的一切，實在是痛心得很。

理想原來是怎樣也追踪不上事實呵！

這是人類社會中的無垠缺陷。

喜峯口下一齣民間悲劇

— 洋洋

喜峰口在華北地勢上，爲兵家所必爭，牠也是長城重要口隘之一，記得直奉兩次内戰，都曾在此處留下莫大的戰績，大樹將軍好像也在其地高揭倒戈旗幟，而發明中華軍閥叛主通敵之風，然在九一八後，宋哲元先生抗日之役，大戰長城間，鏖兵於喜峯口，砲火接天，血肉相搏，尤其器械不精，後無接濟，士卒忍饖耐寒，仍與敵人作殊死戰，其不朽精神，眞能動天地泣鬼神，而爲中華民國對外作戰歷史上留得最光榮之一頁，且爲東北失陷以來差强人意之一頁，尤可見我國軍人並非完全勇於私鬥，而皆對外無抵抗行爲也，昨偶讀元代詩人的一首詩，也是叙述喜峯口的故事，相傳宋未元初有一閩籍靑年士兵，出塞投軍，相從元太祖輾轉作戰，數載杳無消息，其父念子情殷，遂由家鄉跋涉四方，以尋其子，及至喜峯口，居然被他找到，父子一旦相見，樂極生悲，抱頭痛哭，不料一慟俱絶，大約父子二人之精神與軀殼皆含有莫大痛苦，一個間關萬里，一個從軍十年，其心靈上的悲哀和身體上的痛創，皆必密密層層的裏着，所以目的旣達，痛定思痛，就一蹶不可復振了，當時那靑年士兵的主將，發現這幕悲劇，很想替他父子留個紀念，除將他二人屍骨埋葬立碑述事外，特命名其戍地爲『喜逢口』，俾後人顧名思義，得知所以，但是年湮日久，未知如何，改『逢』稱『峯』，地名訛傳，猶其小事，惟此慈父一番天倫之愛，竟永遠埋沒不彰，的確是椿憾事，還有一件可惜的事，這父子倆的姓名未傳，本來他倆的地位太小，中國人從前思想，完全封建化，就因地位太小，又有何人去注意這齣有價値的民間悲劇？如今因事誌名的地方，尙且更改掉，不要説他父子倆的墓與碑自然格外無遺跡可搜尋咧，所幸還有一位姓許的詩人不辭勞苦，曾作同情的悲哀，留了這樣的一篇文字，尙可供給我們想像悼呢詩曰：

『兒解寒衣重撫摩，兒飢推食孰忍呵？長城與國遠負戈，一去不返當如何？去時云出東北鄙，直出榆關度遼水；白頭郎罷與影俱，豈憚山川千萬里。天敎此地適相逢，父曰從天墜吾子，笑疲樂極俱殉身，誰復鍾情遽如此！官家開邊方未已，同生又别寗同死，山雲漠漠風颼颼，山頭雙塚知幾秋？當時不忍一朝　：今日　成千載愁。猶　貞女化爲石，終古孤身　不得！淸江寒影日悠悠，行人一去無消息。』

Page 23

1934.05.19

Transformation of British Far East Policy: Labour Leader Criticizes Government's Appeasement of Japan; Conservatives Still Nostalgic for Old Alliance; Foreign Secretary Simon Explains Nine-Power Treaty, Saying "Respect" and "Guarantee" Are Clearly Different

(London) During today's parliamentary session, Labour leader Clement Attlee spoke, criticizing Japan's policies in the Far East.

The Labour leader's speech denounced Japan, insisting that Japan had begun to implement imperialistic expansion, and Japan's ambition was aimed not at Russia, but at China. Attlee continued that Russia's strength was substantial, so the ambitions of Japanese militarists to penetrate Siberia and reach Lake Baikal seemed somewhat suppressed, and they turned their focus to North China. It is generally recognized that Japan wants to establish a second "Manchukuo" in North China. Will Britain continue to tacitly allow its interests in China to be divided by Japan? It should be known that once Japan annexes North China, it will prepare to gradually encroach upon South China and expel the European powers. It is rumored that Japan has used sweet words to lure Turkey into joining the German-Japanese alliance. If so, a group opposing the League of Nations may be formed, backed by the power of Japan and Germany. During Attlee's speech, Chinese Ambassador Guo Taiqi and other dignitaries were sitting in the audience.

Conservative members frequently express goodwill towards Japan. Conservative MP Keyes then claimed that the Singapore naval base should not be regarded as a threat to Japan, but is closely related to the defenses of New Zealand and Australia. He always regretted the termination of the Anglo-Japanese alliance. If we could reach a thorough and good understanding with Japan, it would be very beneficial to the interests of the Empire and the British in the Far East.

Foreign Secretary Simon, regarding the Nine-Power Treaty and Britain's intention to tear it up, spoke in the House of Commons at 1:37 this afternoon, saying that although Japan's semi-official statement has caused anxiety in many other countries, it is the British government that is negotiating. Since Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota has given a solemn guarantee to British Ambassador Lindley, how can he say to a friendly government, "I don't believe it"? No country has undertaken to use its military force to maintain the territorial integrity and political independence of China. The Nine-Power Treaty only speaks of respecting territorial integrity. Respect and maintain are clearly different. As for whether the League of Nations' handling of the Far East issue is inappropriate, opinions vary. Everyone has their own views.

Reform the League of Nations by first seeking to resolve disarmament. Simon then discussed the reform of the League of Nations, saying that he and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini are both willing to reconsider the League of Nations Covenant. They believe that if this matter is mixed into the already troubled disarmament discussions, it may not lead to a compromise. Any amendment to the Covenant should allow Germany to participate. Britain intends to do its best to help resolve the disarmament issue.

Unwilling to easily implement economic sanctions. Britain is currently closely studying the issue of economic sanctions, but such sanctions, if implemented rashly, will inevitably lead to war. Sanctions should not only be applied to weak countries, but must also be applied to strong countries. Economic pressure, without strength, is ineffective. We deeply appreciate the contributions that the United States has made to the improvement of international affairs, but it must be known that the future actions of the United States have their own scope. It is useless to speculate beyond this scope.

Simon then spoke of the situation in Geneva, refuting the general view that "we have reached the end of a tragic and adventurous undertaking and should strike our tents." He said that if we achieve nothing, the harm to the world would be unimaginable. Simon then added that Great Britain has always been a leader, aiming to achieve disarmament. If the current attempt at disarmament unfortunately fails, it must be followed by new efforts. Simon's speech lasted for an hour, and he then answered Attlee's questions, saying that Great Britain naturally supports the League of Nations' report on the Far East incident and will never deviate from it without proper notice. Simon's last words were, "As long as we are bound by the Nine-Power Treaty, we will do everything in our power to abide by it."

(Reuters telegram, 18th)

(London) The House of Commons debated the Japanese issue fiercely today. Foreign Secretary Simon strongly defended the government's policy toward Japan and replied to the angry questioning of the members, saying that he now wanted to draw the attention of the members to the fact that although Britain had expressed respect for the territorial integrity of China, Britain had not made any guarantee to maintain that integrity. During the debate, Liberal and Labour members accused the government of encouraging Japan's expansion in the Far East, and the British government's response to Japan's declaration of policy toward China was also severely criticized. Labour leader Clement Attlee began today's debate by saying that Japan had posed a serious threat to peace in the Far East and to peace throughout the world. Mr. Cazalet said that, in view of Britain's own actions elsewhere in the world, it is difficult for us to cast the first stone at Japan. The proposed sanctions will not only lead to an Anglo-Japanese war, but will also lead to a Japanese-American war, so we should not threaten Japan. Admiral Keyes advocated a compromise with Japan, saying that Japan inevitably occupies a large part in Eastern affairs and is determined to move forward, so I advocate that the British government should understand Japan well. Then, the agreement on air force disarmament was discussed. Lord President Baldwin made a shocking statement, saying that this agreement must stipulate sanctions against any country that violates it. Such sanctions will inevitably lead to war, so if we want to impose sanctions, we must prepare for war. At present, Britain is already carrying out preliminary plans to expand its air force. Baldwin acknowledged the seriousness of the world situation, but remained confident that Britain would not face any danger in the near future. Baldwin also said that if we want to implement collective security sanctions, we must put Britain in a stronger position. This afternoon, Foreign Secretary Simon also stated in the House of Commons that the failure of the Disarmament Conference is inevitable, but this is not the end of the world. On the day of the disarmament breakdown, we should immediately open another path to devote ourselves to this. It seems too foolish to say that disarmament is like an "anointing ceremony," because Britain will still seek salvation in future conferences (Simon's so-called future conference refers to the League of Nations' General Disarmament Conference on May 29). However, at the next meeting, Britain will no longer put forward proposals, but will only clarify Britain's previous suggestions and ask the representatives of other countries if they have better ideas. (National Telegram, 18th)

New Japanese Policy Towards China: Ariyoshi's Return to Post to Lead to Developments

(Tokyo) The American-run Japan Advertiser stated in today's editorial that the reason why the Japanese Foreign Ministry issued a statement on April 17 prohibiting others from interfering in China was because it knew that the powers were currently considering some concrete methods to revive China. If Japan refuses third countries to assist China in the name of the League of Nations, then it must be able to give China what it does not allow China to receive from other countries' assistance. The Japanese government now seems prepared to do so. Soon, Japan may have its Minister to China, Ariyoshi Akira, announce Japan's action plan. (Reuters telegram, 18th)

Question of Opium in Manchukuo: British Foreign Secretary Simon Answers Member's Question

(London) British Foreign Secretary Simon answered a question from Labour MP Grenfell in the House of Commons today, saying that the League of Nations Opium Committee has not issued a report on the establishment of a state monopoly on opium in the northeastern provinces of China under Japanese military occupation. The British government abides by the recommendations of the Opium Advisory Committee, strictly examines applications to transport narcotics into Manchuria and Jehol, and abides by its obligations under the Hague Peace Convention. (Reuters telegram, 18th)

Japanese People Are Overly Sensitive: Sino-Russian Secret Agreement Is Groundless

According to the TASS news agency's inquiries from all reliable sources, the report transmitted by the Moscow Japanese Union News Agency that the Chinese Ambassador to the Soviet Union, Yan Huiqing, now in Beiping, and the Soviet diplomatic representative in Beiping have concluded a secret agreement on Inner Mongolia is obviously completely nonsense. (TASS telegram, 17th)

Litvinov Arrives in Geneva: New Developments in the Issue of Russia's Accession to the League of Nations

(Geneva) Soviet Russian Foreign Commissar Litvinov will arrive here tonight and will immediately meet with French Foreign Minister Barthou to discuss everything. It is said that what they will discuss is the issue of Soviet Russia's accession to the League of Nations, so it is expected here that important developments will occur soon. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Geneva) Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov has arrived here today. Although he came for the disarmament issue, he has once again aroused general attention to the possibility of Soviet Russia joining the League of Nations. Litvinov is scheduled to meet with French Foreign Minister Barthou this afternoon, and then will visit the League of Nations Italian representative Aloisi and the British representative Eden. Although there are still major difficulties to be eliminated, it is believed that various issues can be resolved satisfactorily at the League of Nations General Assembly in September. Poland and Spain are now advocating that if a permanent council seat is given to Soviet Russia, then this seat should also be given to the two countries. Poland also demands that the rights of minority ethnic groups in treaties should be made universal. It is said that Soviet Russia wants to be invited to join the League of Nations to avoid applying itself and being opposed by others, which would be embarrassing. (Reuters telegram, 18th)

League of Nations Technical Cooperation Council

Passed the Rajchman Report: Confirmed Cooperation Methods to Help China's Construction, Distributed to Technical Agencies for Research, Ambassador Gu Refuted Japan's Unreasonable Opposition, Praising Rajchman for Fulfilling His Responsibilities

(Geneva) On the afternoon of the 17th, the Administrative Yuan's China and League of Nations Technical Cooperation Committee passed the Rajchman Report. The committee will convene another meeting after the League of Nations' various technical organizations have studied the report. (Central News Agency telegram, 17th)

(Nanjing) Foreign news: The China Technical Cooperation Committee held a meeting on the 17th. Our country's representative, Gu Weijun, delivered a speech, the main point being that Rajchman's report was considered faithful and served within the scope of the powers conferred by the League of Nations. This speech refuted the unreasonable opposition of the Japanese side. (Special telegram, 18th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Yuan Technical Cooperation Committee held a meeting and passed the following resolution: The Administrative Yuan Technical Cooperation Committee held a meeting on the 17th to study the Rajchman Report and the detailed documents of the technical representative's work in China from the time of his appointment to April 1 of this year. Rajchman made a brief presentation on the development of technical cooperation between China and the League of Nations. During the exchange of views, the Chinese representative conveyed to the committee the Chinese government's special gratitude for the services of the technical representative and other experts in China, and pointed out that the Chinese government regarded the technical cooperation with various countries through the League of Nations as valuable. The Administrative Yuan Technical Cooperation Committee is aware that the implementation of cooperation between the League of Nations and China is in accordance with the resolutions of May 31, 1931, April 3, 1932, and the Administrative Yuan Technical Cooperation Committee of July 18, 1933, and is pleased to know that the cooperation methods stipulated in the resolutions have benefited China's construction work. The Secretary-General should be requested to forward the technical representative's report to the League of Nations' various technical agencies, and the technical representative should provide all necessary information to the relevant technical agencies and the relevant departments. The Secretary-General should also forward the opinions of the technical agencies to the Administrative Yuan Technical Cooperation Committee at the appropriate time. This report should also be distributed by the Secretary-General to the member states of the Administrative Yuan. (Central News Agency telegram, 18th)

Ambassador Gu's Address

(Geneva) At today's meeting of the League of Nations China Technical Cooperation Committee, Chinese Ambassador to France Dr. Gu Weijun raised a dispute, saying that Dr. Rajchman's report was completely objective, and the current situation in China was accurately recorded in the book. China felt grateful for the assistance given by the League of Nations, and was very pleased that Dr. Rajchman恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪恪

English Policy Shift in the Far East: Labour Leader Criticizes Government's Complacency Towards Japan; Conservatives Still Cling to Old Alliance; Foreign Minister Simon Explains Nine-Power Treaty, Saying There's a Clear Distinction Between Respect and Guarantee

(London) During the House of Commons session today, Labour leader Clement Attlee spoke, criticizing Japan's policies in the Far East.

The Labour leader spoke critically of Japan, insisting that Japan has already embarked on an imperialistic path of expansion, with its sights set on China rather than Russia. Attlee further stated that Russia's substantial power has somewhat curbed the ambitions of Japanese militarists to delve into Siberia as far as Lake Baikal. They have shifted their focus to North China, where Japan's desire to establish a second "Manchukuo" is widely acknowledged. Will Britain continue to tacitly permit the division of its interests in China by Japan? It should be understood that once Japan annexes North China, it will prepare to gradually encroach upon South China and expel the European powers. Rumors suggest that Japan is using sweet words to entice Turkey into joining the German-Japanese alliance. If this occurs, a group opposing the League of Nations may emerge, backed by the strength of Japan and Germany. Chinese Ambassador Guo Taiqi and other key figures were present in the audience during Attlee's speech.

Conservative MPs frequently show favour to Japan. Conservative MP Keyes followed, asserting that the Singapore naval base should not be viewed as a threat to Japan, but rather as closely related to the defense of New Zealand and Australia. He consistently lamented the termination of the Anglo-Japanese Alliance. He believes that a thorough and positive understanding with Japan would greatly benefit the interests of the Empire and the British in the Far East.

Foreign Minister Simon, on Britain's intent to tear up the Nine-Power Treaty, delivered a speech in the House of Commons at 1:37 PM today, stating that while Japan's semi-official declaration has caused anxiety in many other countries, the British government is the one engaging in negotiations. Since Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota has offered a solemn guarantee to British Ambassador Lindley, how can he state to a friendly government, "I don't believe it"? No nation has undertaken the obligation to use its military force to uphold the territorial integrity and political independence of China. The Nine-Power Treaty only mentions respecting territorial integrity. There is a clear distinction between "respect" and "maintain." As for whether the League of Nations has mishandled the Far East issue, opinions vary and each has their own perspective.

Reform the League of Nations by First Seeking Disarmament. Simon then discussed reforming the League of Nations, stating that he and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini are both willing to reconsider the League of Nations Covenant. They believe that incorporating this issue into the already complex discussions on disarmament would likely hinder achieving a compromise. Any amendment to the Covenant should include German participation. Britain intends to exert every effort to facilitate the resolution of the disarmament issue.

Unwilling to Easily Implement Economic Sanctions. Britain is currently closely studying the issue of economic sanctions. However, such sanctions, if implemented recklessly, would inevitably lead to war. Sanctions should not only be applied to weak countries, but must also be applied to strong countries. Economic pressure is ineffective without force. We deeply appreciate the contributions that the United States has made to the improvement of international affairs, but it must be understood that the future actions of the United States are bound by its own scope. It is useless to speculate beyond this scope.

Simon then spoke about the situation in Geneva, refuting the general sentiment that "we have reached the end of a tragic and adventurous undertaking and should strike our tents." He said that if we achieve nothing, the harm to the world would be unimaginable. Simon then added that Great Britain has always been a leader, aiming to achieve disarmament. If the current attempt at disarmament unfortunately fails, it must be followed by new efforts. Simon's speech lasted for an hour, after which he responded to Attlee's inquiry, stating that Great Britain naturally supports the League of Nations' report on the Far East incident and will never depart from it without appropriate notification. Simon concluded by saying, "As long as we are bound by the Nine-Power Treaty, we will do everything in our power to abide by it."

(Reuters telegram, 18th)

(London) The House of Commons debated the Japan issue heatedly today. Foreign Secretary Simon strongly defended the government's policy towards Japan and responded to the angry questions of the members by saying that he again wanted to call the attention of the members to the fact that although Britain had expressed respect for the territorial integrity of China, Britain had not made any guarantee to maintain that integrity. During the debate, Liberal and Labour members condemned the government for encouraging Japan's territorial expansion in the Far East, and the British government's response to Japan's declaration of policy towards China was also severely criticized. Labour leader Clement Attlee initiated today's debate by stating that Japan had posed a serious threat to peace in the Far East and to world peace. Mr. Cazalet stated that, considering Britain's own actions elsewhere in the world, it is difficult for us to cast the first stone at Japan. The proposed sanctions would not only lead to an Anglo-Japanese war, but would also trigger a Japanese-American war, so we should not threaten Japan. Admiral Keyes advocated compromise with Japan, stating that Japan inevitably occupies a significant role in Eastern affairs and is determined to move forward. Therefore, I advocate that the British government should understand Japan well. The discussion then turned to the Air Force disarmament agreement, during which Lord President Baldwin made a startling statement, stating that the agreement must stipulate sanctions against any nation that violates it. Such sanctions would inevitably lead to war, so if we wish to impose sanctions, we must prepare for war. Currently, Britain has already begun preliminary plans to expand its air force. Baldwin acknowledged the seriousness of the world situation, but remains confident that Britain will not face any immediate danger. Baldwin also stated that if we wish to implement collective security sanctions, Britain must be placed in a stronger position. This afternoon, Foreign Secretary Simon also stated in the House of Commons that the failure of the Disarmament Conference is inevitable, but this is not the end of the world. On the day of the disarmament collapse, we must immediately seek new avenues to dedicate ourselves to it. It would be foolish to consider disarmament a "Requiem," as Britain will continue to seek a resolution at future conferences (Simon's future conferences refer to the League of Nations Disarmament General Assembly on May 29). However, at the next conference, Britain will no longer put forward proposals, but will only clarify its previous suggestions and seek feedback from representatives of other nations on whether they have better ideas. (National Telegram, 18th)

New Japanese Policy Towards China: Ariyoshi's Reappointment Will Bring Developments

(Tokyo) Today's editorial in the American-run Japan Advertiser stated that the reason why the Japanese Foreign Ministry issued a statement on April 17, prohibiting others from interfering in China, was that it knew the great powers were currently considering concrete methods to revive China. If Japan refuses to allow third countries to assist China under the auspices of the League of Nations, then it must provide China with that which it denies China from receiving from other nations. It seems the Japanese government is now prepared to do so. Soon, Japan's Minister to China, Ariyoshi Akira, may announce Japan's action plan. (Reuters Telegram, 18th)

Question of Opium in Manchukuo: British Foreign Minister Simon Answers Member's Question

(London) Today, British Foreign Minister Simon answered Labour MP Grenfell's question in the House of Commons, stating that the League of Nations Opium Committee has not issued a report on the establishment of a state opium monopoly in China's northeastern provinces under Japanese military occupation. The British government abides by the recommendations of the Opium Advisory Committee, rigorously examines applications to transport narcotics into Manchuria and Jehol, and adheres to the obligations under the Hague Peace Convention. (Reuters Telegram, 18th)

Japanese Overreaction: Sino-Russian Secret Agreement is Nonsense

According to inquiries from all reliable sources by TASS, the report circulated by the Moscow Japanese League News Agency that Yan Huiqing, the Chinese Ambassador to the Soviet Union, currently in Beiping, and the Soviet diplomatic representative in Beiping have concluded a secret agreement regarding Inner Mongolia, is clearly utter nonsense. (TASS telegram, 17th)

Litvinov Arrives in Geneva: New Developments to Occur in the Question of Russia's Admission to the League of Nations

(Geneva) Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov will arrive here tonight and will immediately meet with French Foreign Minister Barthou to discuss all matters. It is said that what they will discuss is the issue of Soviet Russia's accession to the League of Nations, so it is expected here that important developments will occur soon. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Geneva) Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov has arrived here today. Although his visit is related to the disarmament issue, it has once again drawn general attention to the possibility of Soviet Russia joining the League of Nations. Litvinov is scheduled to meet with French Foreign Minister Barthou this afternoon, followed by visits to the League of Nations Italian representative Aloisi and British representative Eden. Although significant difficulties remain to be resolved, it is believed that various issues can be resolved satisfactorily at the League of Nations General Assembly in September. Poland and Spain are now advocating that if a permanent council seat is given to Soviet Russia, then this seat should also be granted to both countries. Poland also demands that treaty-based minority rights should be made universal. It is heard that Soviet Russia prefers to be widely invited to join the League of Nations to avoid applying itself and facing opposition, which would be embarrassing. (Reuters Telegram, 18th)

League of Nations Technical Cooperation Committee

Passed the Rajchman Report: Cooperation Methods to Assist China's Construction Confirmed, Distributed to Technical Agencies for Research, Ambassador Gu Refutes Japan's Unjustified Opposition, Praising Rajchman for Fulfilling his Responsibilities

(Geneva) In the afternoon of the 17th, the Executive Yuan's Committee on Technical Cooperation between China and the League of Nations passed the Rajchman Report. The committee will convene another meeting after the League of Nations' various technical organizations have studied the report. (Central News Agency telegram, 17th)

(Nanjing) Foreign news: The China Technical Cooperation Committee held a meeting on the 17th. Our country's representative, Gu Weijun, delivered a speech, the main points of which were that Rajchman's report was considered faithful and served within the scope of the authority given to him by the League of Nations. This speech refuted Japan's unreasonable opposition. (Special telegram, 18th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council's Technical Cooperation Committee held a meeting and passed the following resolution: The Administrative Council's Technical Cooperation Committee held a meeting on the 17th to study the Rajchman Report and the detailed documents of the technical representative's work in China from the time of his appointment to April 1 of this year. Rajchman made a brief presentation on the development of technical cooperation between China and the League of Nations. During the exchange of views, the Chinese representative conveyed to the committee the Chinese government's special gratitude for the services of the technical representative and other experts in China, and specifically pointed out that the Chinese government considered its technical cooperation with various countries through the League of Nations as valuable. The Administrative Council's Technical Cooperation Committee is aware that the implementation of cooperation between the League of Nations and China is in accordance with the resolutions of May 31, 1931, April 3, 1932, and the Administrative Council's Technical Cooperation Committee of July 18, 1933, and is pleased to know that the cooperation methods stipulated in the resolutions have benefited China's construction work. The Secretary-General should be requested to forward the technical representative's report to the League of Nations' various technical agencies, and the technical representative should provide all necessary information to the relevant technical agencies and departments. The Secretary-General should also forward the opinions of the technical agencies to the Administrative Council's Technical Cooperation Committee at the appropriate time. This report should also be distributed by the Secretary-General to the member states of the Administrative Council. (Central News Agency telegram, 18th)

Truth Behind the Shooting of a Finance Ministry Employee Still Under Investigation

(Nanjing) Regarding the case of Finance Ministry employee Huo Ziduan being shot by a railway police officer, Huo is in good condition after being hospitalized and having the bullet removed. According to Deng Liangsheng, secretary of the Railway Police Bureau, Director Sun Lida of the railway police unit reported the incident to the bureau on the 17th, stating that immediately after the incident, the station military police checked the railway police's bullets and found none missing. An examination of the gun muzzle also showed no signs of firing. Therefore, it is believed that the bullet did not come from the railway police, leaving its origin a mystery. The situation has been reported to the Shanghai Police Department by telegram. If the bullet was fired by the railway police, the railway police will bear responsibility. The bullet is currently at the hospital, and its origin can be proven once the bullet is jointly examined. However, the bureau has not received an official report, so it is difficult to predict how to handle the matter. Liang Chenkai, the deputy director of the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway Police Department, arrived in Beijing on the 18th to investigate the truth of the case. (18th Special Dispatch)

Roosevelt Orders Investigation

Japanese Goods Invading American Markets; Investigation into Imports of Japanese Porcelain and Pottery; There is a Growing Trend to Emulate British Boycott of Japanese Goods

(Washington) Due to the fierce competition of Japanese goods in the American market, there are numerous criticisms from all sides. President Roosevelt specifically ordered the Tariff Commission today to investigate whether the current imports of porcelain and pottery are harming domestic products. Roosevelt is extremely concerned about domestic products because domestic production costs have increased in accordance with the National Recovery Administration industry regulations. According to responsible sources, if the Tariff Commission finds that these imports are harming American products, President Roosevelt will use his unlimited powers under the Recovery Act to immediately restrict imports. (17th National Telegram)

(New York) There is a growing trend in the United States to emulate Britain's restrictions on textile imports. If this happens, Japan will be severely hit. The American Cotton Textile Industry Regulations authorities submitted a request to the Tariff Commission today to immediately investigate the extent to which foreign goods are invading the domestic market, advocating for the adoption of full measures to prevent the invasion of foreign goods. There has been a constant outcry that countries with low living standards are exporting large quantities of cotton and other textiles to the United States, causing significant losses to domestic industries. Therefore, the industry regulations authorities have specifically drawn the Tariff Commission's attention to this issue. At the same time, Japan has taken the first official step in London, requesting the British government to revise its policy of limiting Japanese goods entering Britain. Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira sent a diplomatic note to British Trade Minister Runciman, stating the Japanese government's views on the new quota and raising the question of whether the new British quota violates the most-favored-nation treatment clause in the Anglo-Japanese commercial treaty. This note requested the British government to reconsider the quota, but did not mention how Japan would respond. The British Trade Minister agreed to consider the note. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

(New York) According to reliable sources here today, the US government has commissioned an investigation into the DuPont Armaments Factory's sale of a large number of ammonia nitrate machinery to Japan. It is reported that US government officials had informally questioned the DuPont factory about the sale of the latest ammonia nitrate manufacturing machinery to Mitsui & Co. of Japan, based on the fact that certain items licensed by the United States are not allowed to be exported. Factory officials stated in response that there was nothing shady about the sale of this machinery, because such machinery could also be purchased from other countries. They also stated that if the factory had refused the sale, Mitsui & Co. could have purchased it from Germany. Currently, this machinery is purely for agricultural purposes and cannot be forcibly labeled as military use. After discussion by the Washington administrative authorities, the factory was notified that the authorities would no longer object and that the factory could continue to sell to Japan. However, newspapers have widely reported on the matter, claiming that this machinery could be converted for military use. Therefore, the factory's Washington office issued a statement purely from an agricultural and commercial standpoint, stating that Japan has limited farmland and that its farmers urgently need this machinery to increase production, as Japan needs to produce its own fertilizers. (17th National Telegram)

Matsudaira Lodges Protest Against British Exclusion of Japanese Goods; British Trade Minister Will Soon Issue a Reply; No Revision Expected for Boycott Measures

(London) Since last Monday, after Trade Minister Runciman announced in the House of Commons that the colonies would adopt measures to restrict the quantity of imported cotton textiles and rayon from foreign countries, the Japanese government has regarded this move as a violation of the most-favored-nation clause.

This afternoon, Japanese Ambassador to the UK Matsudaira visited Trade Minister Runciman at the Ministry of Trade and had a lengthy conversation. Matsudaira informed Runciman of the Japanese government's opinion, stating that Anglo-Japanese commercial relations have always been based on most-favored-nation treatment, and that the recent restrictions imposed by British colonies on the import of Japanese goods are contrary to the most-favored-nation clause. Runciman took note of the Japanese Ambassador's opinion. However, it is said that Runciman replied to Matsudaira that, in his view, the most-favored-nation clause should not be interpreted in this way, and that the measures taken by the UK apply equally to all countries and do not violate commercial treaties. It is likely that the British government will not consider the Japanese request to be valid, and that the British government's recent measures, except for some minor details, will not be revised in any way. Runciman will soon send the British reply to Matsudaira. (17th Havas Dispatch)

(London) The Silk Problems Advisory Committee, commissioned to study the revision of tariffs on imported foreign silk fabrics, has recently submitted its report. This matter is closely related to the Anglo-French commercial negotiations. This evening, Trade Minister Runciman met with French Ambassador Corbin to inform him of the contents of the report and to explain the British government's recent formal measures regarding Japanese imports. Runciman and Corbin then jointly studied the current state of Anglo-French commercial negotiations and considered what methods could be used to enable economic experts from both countries to quickly reopen discussions in London. (17th Havas Dispatch)

Japanese Delegation Departs for Dutch-Japanese Trade Conference

(Tokyo) The Japanese government representatives attending the Dutch-Japanese conference in Batavia, including Chief Representative Nagaoka Haruichi, advisors Kimura Eiichi and Yamanaka Seizaburo, and other accompanying personnel, departed from Tokyo Station at 9:25 this morning. Representative Nagaoka told reporters in the train that the Japanese delegation's attitude towards the Dutch-Japanese conference is like a blank sheet of paper. After attending the conference, they will respond to any proposals from the Dutch side on an ad hoc basis. The conference should reach a goal through mutual concessions. Of course, I will act in accordance with Japanese public opinion when attending the conference. After arriving in Osaka, I plan to meet with Osaka business people to listen to their opinions for reference. (18th Japanese United Press Dispatch)

The government delegation attending the Dutch-Japanese conference in Osaka met with cotton manufacturers this morning and held consultations. The manufacturers presented a memorandum to Chief Representative Nagaoka, which contained the steps to be taken at the conference: (1) Nagaoka should try to get the Netherlands to abolish import restrictions on Japanese cotton goods, except for bleached goods; (2) An agreement should be established that bleached goods directly shipped from Japan to the Dutch East Indies should be in accordance with the amount in 1933; (3) The import license system in the Dutch East Indies should be abolished. The Japanese delegation is scheduled to leave Kobe tomorrow, taking the route through Singapore to Batavia. (18th [Illegible] Dispatch)

Roosevelt Will Submit Five Messages to Congress; Silver Bill Will Prompt International Conference

(Washington) The White House announced today that President Roosevelt will submit five special messages to Congress within a week. Congressional leaders are currently clearing everything in preparation for formally rejecting or approving various bills. The President's five messages are as follows:

(1) War Debts - It is expected that President Roosevelt will only make a report on the current state of European war debts and does not want to request broad powers at this time to reduce or amend the debts of various countries.

(2) Silver - This message will be submitted on Sunday. The President and silver faction leaders have reached a compromise agreement. President Roosevelt has agreed to propose in his special message a mandatory and permissible bill that he is willing to accept.

(3) Arms - President Roosevelt will request Congress to appoint a special committee to investigate the activities of arms companies during the congressional recess and to propose opinions on the management of arms. The President will also request the power to order a ban on the shipment of arms to Bolivia and Paraguay, in order to stop the Chaco War.

(4) Coconut Oil Tax - President Roosevelt opposes incorporating the 3% coconut oil tax into the tax amendment recently passed by Congress. However, the President will be forced to sign the bill because he does not want to veto the entire bill because of this one point.

(5) Social Issues - This message will address in detail the various social problems arising from the depression, such as slum clearance, housing, federal government prevention of criminal behavior, poverty relief, pensions, worker compensation, and unemployment insurance. House Majority Leader Byrns said that the President has abandoned the idea of passing labor laws in this session of Congress. (17th National Telegram)

(Washington) It is generally expected that after the silver legislation is enacted in the future, the result may be that silver discussions will start again at the World Economic Conference. Silver faction Senator King predicted today that an international expert conference could be convened within a year. (17th Reuters Dispatch)

French Defense Budget

(Paris) The French defense budget has been widely known after being discussed by Finance Minister Germain-Martin and Army Minister Pétain. The budget was submitted to the lower house on April 28 of this year and is now only awaiting approval from the finance committee of the lower house. The total amount of the expenses is 30 billion francs, of which 1,011,000,000 francs are earmarked for the completion of border forts from 1934 to 1935. For the naval expenses from 1934 to 1938, the Minister of the Navy proposed 825,000,000 francs for the construction of oil pools, coastal defense, and naval aviation equipment. The aviation ministry will need 980,000,000 francs this year to purchase air force equipment and add fighter planes. (17th National News Agency Dispatch)

Results of US Naval Simulation; Proves Fleet Has Strength to Defend Canal; Enemy Will Pay a Heavy Price to Occupy or Destroy It

Balboa Heights, Panama Canal Zone According to Senior Military Officials, the Lessons Learned by the Naval Authorities in this Tactical Exercise Are Very Valuable. This Exercise Began on April 9 When the US Fleet Departed from San Pedro and Ended When It Arrived in Balboa Heights. An Associated Press Reporter Learned Today of the Three Significant Results of This Exercise:

(1) The Panama Canal Can Theoretically Be Occupied or Destroyed by an Enemy Fleet, but the Price Would Be Too High for Even the Strongest Country to Bear, so Actual Occupation is Impossible. (2) Under the Current Situation, a Japanese-American Naval War Is Completely Impossible. Although Enemy Forces Can Land on the Mainland with a Large Naval Force, Any Attempt to Seize the Canal with a Smaller Fleet is Tantamount to Suicide. (3) Due to the Above Facts, Battleships Have Become the Main Force in Defending the Panama Canal.

This exercise aimed to defend the Panama Canal and the eastern United States when the US Fleet Was Caught Off Guard at the Outbreak of War. It Also Assumed That Enemy Forces Could Occupy a Forward Base in the West Indies and Concentrate a Strong Fleet in the Caribbean Sea. The Exercise Strove to Simulate Actual War Conditions. Navy Secretary Swanson Today Congratulated US Fleet Commander-in-Chief Sellers via Radio for the Success. Acting Chief of Naval Operations Du Shimei Also Praised It, Saying That Considering the Age of Most of the Ships, the Results of This Exercise Were Indeed Rare and Valuable Because Most of the Battleships Have Reached Their Ship Age, and so on. (17th National Telegram)

Saar Issue

League of Nations Has Three Issues Pending Resolution; Requesting Concessions from Both Germany and France; Guaranteeing Individual Freedom of Voting

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council Has Three Important Issues Pending Resolution During This Session: (1) Organizing an International Police Force to Maintain Order and Guarantee Freedom of Voting in the Saar Region During and Around the Time of Next Year's Vote; (2) Guaranteeing the Lives of Residents After the Vote, Which Is Extremely Difficult Because Germany Has Expressed Opposition to Establishing a Special System to Protect Minorities; (3) Determining the Date of the Vote. (17th Havas Dispatch)

(Paris) According to a News Report in Jiji Shinpo Today, the Chairman of the Two-Person Committee of the League of Nations Preparing for the Saar Region Plebiscite, Aloisi, Has Requested Both German and French Members to Make Concessions to Each Other. It Is Said That Aloisi's View Is That Germany Should Give a Solemn Guarantee That All People in the Saar Region Should Have Absolute Individual Freedom of Voting, and That No Retaliatory Measures Should Be Taken Against People Who Vote Against Restoring German National Sovereignty. Furthermore, Guarantees Should Also Be Given to the Saar Minority. If Germany Can Acknowledge the Above Points, Then France and the League of Nations Should Immediately Abandon Their Proposal to Organize an International Police Force. (17th National Telegram)

Saar Governing Council Publishes Response to German Document: Improper Administrative Actions Criticized by Germany as Deviating from the Spirit of Governance

(Geneva) Today, the Secretariat of the League of Nations re-released a letter from the Saar Governing Council to the League of Nations. This letter is the Council's response to the speech given by German Propaganda Minister Goebbels in Ziegenbrück recently. Goebbels' speech contained many criticisms of the Council's administrative actions. One of the strongest points of Germany's criticism of the Council is that many German exiles and political prisoners who have fled to the Saar region are working in the Saar press, engaged in anti-German activities and the propagation of Marxism, and that the Governing Council has even hired some of them. This is contrary to the spirit of the League of Nations' administration of the region. Furthermore, some of the political prisoners have committed ordinary criminal offenses, and the Saar government has recklessly accepted them, which is also inconsistent with the Council's mission. This matter was formally protested by German Foreign Minister Neurath to the Governing Council on February 27. The Council's response is that it has investigated all persons entering the region who are suspected of criminal activity. However, officials of the Council who were forced to leave their positions after Germany implemented the new civil service law cannot all be regarded as exiles. It is expected that Germany will regard this response as a refusal to consider Germany's protest. (National Telegram, 18th)

U.S. Cooperates with League of Nations to Prevent Chaco War: President to Ask Congress to Legislate Arms Embargo

(Washington) Today, Under Secretary of State Phillips stated that President Roosevelt may ask Congress to immediately pass an arms embargo, as Geneva has been discussing a worldwide ban on arms shipments to Bolivia and Paraguay. Phillips declared that the United States is prepared to cooperate with the League of Nations to prevent the Chaco War, but President Roosevelt can only issue the embargo after Congress grants this authority. Both the Senate and House of Representatives have passed a joint resolution authorizing the President to prohibit arms exports. The resolution has been amended by the Senate and is awaiting House approval. The President's actions are based on the proposal of the League of Nations Council, as League representatives have stated that the feasibility of banning arms to Bolivia and Paraguay depends on whether the United States is willing to join the embargo agreement. The U.S. congressional joint resolution has been delayed due to the Senate amendment, which stipulates that the arms export ban should be implemented simultaneously against both belligerent countries. Therefore, this amendment may hinder the United States or the international community from imposing sanctions on aggressor countries. (National Telegram, 17th)

Central Government Holds Memorial Meeting for Chen Qimei's Martyrdom: Ye Chucang Reports on the Life of Martyr Chen

(Nanjing) The Central Government held a memorial meeting for the martyrdom of the late Chen Qimei at 9:00 AM on the 18th. Attendees included Central Committee members Ye Chucang, Li Cizhun, Deng Jiayan, Chen Shuren, Chu Minyi, Li Zonghuang, Xie Zuomin, Liu Shouzhong, Zhang Ji, Wang Luyi, Chen Ce, Ji Liang, Zhou Qigang, Xiao Jishan, Wang Qi, Chuan Rulin, and representatives from various agencies, including Chen Qicai, Chen Rui, Cheng Ji'an, Wang Qijiang, and staff members, totaling 600 people. Chairman Ye Chucang led the attendees in paying respects and laying wreaths. Since Ju Zheng was out of the capital on official business, Ye Chucang gave a temporary report, briefly stating that Mr. Chen Qimei's great achievements during his lifetime and the circumstances of his martyrdom are well known and need not be repeated. However, Mr. Chen Qimei had three special qualities that we should emulate: (1) Mr. Chen Qimei was extremely intelligent, but he dedicated it to the Party and the country and never used his intelligence for his own private gain; (2) He pursued any cause that he believed was beneficial to the Party and the country, regardless of criticism, praise, or hardship, and would not stop until it was accomplished; (3) The more dangerous the situation, the more calm and composed he was, never evading but stepping forward to face it. Mr. Chen Qimei's special spirit is difficult for us to learn, but we must learn it. Otherwise, even if we only learn a little, it will be of great benefit to the Party and the country. The meeting adjourned at 9:40 AM. (Central News Agency Telegram, 18th)

(Nanjing) More than 300 representatives from all walks of life in the capital held a memorial meeting for Chen Qimei's martyrdom at the city's Party headquarters on the morning of the 18th. Zhou Bomin, the chairman of the city's executive committee, presided over the meeting and delivered an opening speech, hoping to emulate the spirit of the martyrs who sacrificed and struggled for the nation, to uplift the morale of the people, and to save the country from danger and ruin. Embassy Upgrading Issue: Japan Has Not Yet Formally Proposed It

According to diplomatic sources, Japan does have intentions regarding the upgrading of the Chinese and Japanese embassies. Observing its intentions, there are indeed two levels of significance. First, it will use this to show respect for China's status in order to ease anti-Japanese sentiment. Second, it will use this to show that the problems between China and Japan have become closer, in order to shake the friendly beliefs of various countries towards China. Judging from Japan's various propaganda efforts in recent days, it is quite credible. But in fact, Japanese officials have not yet made a request, and our government has not yet considered it. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Strictly Prohibits Narcotics

(Nanjing) Chairman Chiang Kai-shek believes that in recent years, potent narcotics such as morphine and heroin have been sold and trafficked, flooding various places along the Yangtze River. Unscrupulous merchants smuggle them, and military and police shield them. The harm they cause threatens the extinction of the nation. Although various prohibitions and punishments have been enacted in the past, the regulations and penalties have been too light. In order to eliminate evil completely, he has now specially re-enacted the Provisional Regulations on the Strict Prohibition of Potent Narcotics and issued a circular to the provincial and municipal governments, urging them to strictly comply with them. After receiving the telegram, the Beijing Municipal Government has forwarded it to its subordinates for implementation. (Central News Agency Telegram, 18th)

Comparison of World Air Forces: France First, England Second, U.S. Fourth, Japan Sixth

(New York) According to the U.S. Aviation Chamber of Commerce's forecast, in 1934, the world's aviation industry, including civil and military use and reserve aircraft, will have a high-speed expansion. The Chamber of Commerce's annual report states that in terms of the development of flight technology, the operation of commercial aircraft, and the inheritance of naval and military aircraft, the United States is the champion of the world. However, in terms of the number of fighter jets that can be mobilized immediately, the United States ranks only fourth. The first place is France, with 4,000 aircraft (statistics for December 1933).

The second is England, with 2,500 aircraft, the third is Italy, with 2,300 aircraft, the fourth is the United States, with 1,700 aircraft, the fifth is Soviet Russia, with 2,200 aircraft, of which 1,200 are no longer applicable, and the sixth is Japan, with 1,500 aircraft, of which 300 are not applicable. (Havas Telegram, 17th)

Marseille The French giant aircraft "Arc-en-Ciel," piloted by the famous aviator Mermoz, carrying six passengers, departed from the airport near here at 5:16 this morning to fly to Natal, Brazil, in South America. It is expected to arrive at Casablanca, Morocco, in Africa at noon, make a brief stop, and then proceed to Saint-Louis, Senegal, in French Senegal, and attempt to cross the Atlantic Ocean from there to Natal. It is reported that the "Arc-en-Ciel" aircraft will be used by Air France to fly between South America and Africa. However, before the company officially accepts the aircraft as qualified, it must first fly back and forth three times. This is the first flight. (Havas Telegram, 18th)

Latvian Coalition Cabinet Established: Prime Minister Ulmanis Concurrently Serves as Foreign Minister: First Seeks to Eliminate Domestic Economic Instability

Riga The Latvian government today formed a national unity government, with Ulmanis as Prime Minister and concurrently serving as Foreign Minister. The cabinet members are all experts, each holding special positions, without distinction of political parties. The first step of the new cabinet is to eliminate the economic difficulties that have caused national unrest. This move requires declaring a national state of emergency. The army is now assisting the police to maintain order in the capital. In the past two days, several members of a certain extremist faction and the Social Democratic Party have been arrested, because a large amount of arms hidden by the reactionaries was discovered. These people have threatened to hold a general strike and armed resistance against the government. (Reuters Telegram, 17th)

U.S. Airship Sets Highest Record

Bridgeport, U.S. The American Sikorsky airship S-42 today carried a load of 11,023 tons and rose to an altitude of 21,800 feet, breaking the previous record. It is reported that the previous highest record was 6,561 feet, which was created by a German airship in 1927. (Reuters Telegram, 17th)

Opening of the Fascist Parliament in Vienna: Sixty-Four Members Representing Seven Vocational Groups

Vienna: Vienna Mayor Schmitz solemnly held the opening ceremony of the Vienna City Council today. In the name of the new council, he vowed that all actions would only be for the happiness of Vienna and Austria. He stated that the council is the first public body in Austria to comply with the principles of the new constitution, and therefore, it can not only set an example for Austria but also be a model for other countries with political disorder that need new remedies. Mr. Schmitz also praised the achievements of Prime Minister Dollfuss, who was also present. It is reported that the council is organized in a Fascist style, with members belonging to the seven vocational groups listed in the constitution, totaling sixty-four people. Only seven members are from the old council, and the rest are new members, including four women. Although Catholics are in the majority, Christians and Jews also have representatives participating. It is further reported that the old council was organized with representatives from political parties, with a total of one hundred members. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

Flying Train Successfully Tested in Soviet Russia: Travels Over 500 Miles in Ten Hours

(Moscow) The so-called "flying train" has been successfully test-flown today. Today, the plane flew from Saratov to Moscow, a total distance of 520 miles, taking more than ten hours. It stopped five times en route. Due to weather conditions, it only flew in the evenings and at dusk. The flying train consists of one aircraft towing two gliders. (Reuters dispatch, 17th)

International Commercial Telegraph

Special Commercial News Telegram from Reuters, May 18th: Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: The London gold price today is 136 shillings and 3 pence, 1 pence higher than yesterday.

London Silver: In the London silver market this morning, China sold off, and when the price fell, both China and speculators bought in. Spot is quoted at 19 and 375 pence, down 3.125; futures are at 19 and 4375 pence, down 2.5. The market closed stable.

New York Silver: The silver market is stable, with some buying interest in July futures. Market interest is low, but sentiment is pleasant. The price is slightly higher than London, but the mood is still cheerful. Bombay Silver: The Bombay silver market is closed today.

Exchange Rates

Anglo-American: The London foreign exchange market saw very little trading this morning due to the upcoming holiday. The opening exchange rate for Anglo-American was 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 1 and 125/1000 cents, which is 125/1000 cents higher than yesterday's closing rate for American-British exchange. There were no changes before noon. At 1:00 PM, it rose to 0625, reaching 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 1 and 1875/10000 cents.

Anglo-French: The opening exchange rate was 77 francs and 21 centimes, the same as yesterday's closing price. This price remained unchanged until closing.

American-British: The opening exchange rate for American-British was 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 1 and 125/1000 cents, an increase of 125/1000 cents from yesterday's closing price. It then rose another 125/1000 cents to 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 1 and 25/1000 cents. However, at 10:45 AM, it fell 25/100 cents to 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 1 cent.

American-French: The opening exchange rate for American-French today was 6.62.00.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The cotton market opened slightly weaker due to overnight selling and profit-taking, and the weather reports were favorable for cotton planting. Buyers expressed a wait-and-see attitude because the silver news is not being given much importance now. Sentiment is showing a rebound.

Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market closed stable today. Initially, it fell due to profit-taking, but then it rose due to speculation driven by buying and news from Liverpool. The price for Bai Luo cotton for July/August delivery was 197 rupees, down 25. British Cotton: In the Liverpool cotton market at 1:00 PM, July futures rose 3 pounds to 5.97.

British Wheat: The price of July futures in the Liverpool wheat market was 4 shillings and 5 and 75/100 pence, the same as yesterday's price.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was quiet this morning. At noon, the trading price for July/September futures was 6.25 pence, up 0.0625.

New York: The New York rubber market opened only moderately stable, with mixed sentiment. Market conditions were quiet. Merchants sold, and retail investors bought, but later it became quiet. Merchants waited and watched for developments. The price was slightly closer to London.

Securities

The New York stock market opened stable, and sentiment was more cheerful. The trend was mostly upward because the sense of inflation and the development of the silver issue were still being taken into account. However, trade news was not particularly encouraging. Later, trading gradually eased, and frequent profit-taking caused mixed market conditions. The price of American Metallurgical shares fell by one pound. Orders

On the 18th, the National Government ordered that Liu Yuanju, advisor to the Ministry of Justice Administration, be relieved of his post for other appointments. This order also appointed Liu Yuanju as Director of the Civil Affairs Department of the Ministry of Justice Administration and Chen Fumin as an advisor. This order also ordered that Zhou Xiangxian, Chairman of the Yangtze River Waterway Improvement Committee of the Ministry of Transportation, be relieved of his post for other appointments. This order also appointed Zhao Zhiyou as Chairman of the Yangtze River Waterway Improvement Committee of the Ministry of Transportation.

Conference of Chinese and Japanese Representatives at Shanhaiguan: Yin Tong About to Go to Beijing and Shanghai to Consult on Policy

Beijing Correspondence: The Sino-Japanese problem has been unresolved for a long time. The Japanese have used various methods of intimidation and enticement to achieve their ultimate goals. Our side is under accumulated pressure and finds it difficult to cope. Last month, Huang Fu went south to discuss matters, and Sino-Japanese diplomacy has gradually developed over the past month. For example, various issues in the war zone are seeking appropriate solutions. On the 14th of this month, Chinese and Japanese representatives gathered at Yuguan for another meeting. The Chinese representatives were Yin Rugeng and Tao Shangming, Yin Tong, and the Japanese representatives were Matsui, Director of the Chengde Special Service Agency; Ii, Director of the Yuyu Special Service Agency; Shibayama, Military Attaché of the Japanese Embassy; and Ota Hisakazu, Director of the Puppet Fengshan Railway Bureau. The two sides discussed ways to resolve various issues in the war zone. Ota has already returned east after the meeting, and Yin Tong has also returned to Tianjin. He will go to Beijing and Shanghai within days to consult with the central government and Huang Fu. Tai Yuan, who is in Peiping, will go to Tianjin in the next day or two to have further contact with Yin Tong. As for the various issues in the war zone, the solutions have been discussed and agreed upon at the Yuguan meeting and are now being implemented separately. Yin Rugeng and Shibayama also returned to Peiping yesterday (16th) and immediately contacted the relevant parties. This morning (17th), Yin visited Shibayama again at the Japanese Embassy to discuss the withdrawal of Japanese troops from Jixian County. Shibayama has sent personnel to Jixian this afternoon (17th) to investigate the truth and work together to resolve the issue. Yin has also sent Qu Shihe to handle the matter as appropriate. According to Yin, "The issue of the Japanese troops' intrusion into Jixian County has been resolved very satisfactorily through negotiations with the Japanese side, and it will not be expanded. The Japanese troops who invaded Jixian County are 200 men from the regiment led by Hayashida. A part of them had already withdrawn to Ma Lan Yu the day before yesterday. The rest were originally scheduled to withdraw yesterday, but due to the instigation of traitors, it was said that the militia in the first district of Jixian County were carrying heavy weapons, which caused a misunderstanding by the Japanese troops and delayed the withdrawal. Our side is now negotiating with the Japanese side on whether the militia are carrying heavy weapons. This still needs to be investigated. Even if it is true, we only need to confiscate them ourselves, without the need for external intervention, to avoid causing other disputes. The Japanese side also understands this quite well and has sent Qu Shihe to handle it today, and it should be resolved within a few days. The issue of receiving Ma Lan Yu still involves other matters, which can be carried out when Chairman Huang returns to Peiping. The issue of the puppet police at Gubeikou Nantianmen has been largely resolved and can be withdrawn within days." According to Shibayama, "The Sino-Japanese representatives discussed at the Yuguan meeting only the issues of security administration in the war zone and the continued reception of the remaining ports. The security team in the war zone was a temporary measure, temporarily reorganized from the army. Now the newly formed security team has completed training and can be replaced within a month. At the Yuguan meeting, it was decided that the total number of the security team would be 8,000. Except for the units of Dou Xizhe, Zhou Yuying, and Wei Yonghe, which were transferred out, the unit of Li Jichun was reorganized into the units of Zhao Zhilei and Liu Zuozhou, which will remain in the war zone. The new security team is not allowed to carry heavy weapons. During the change of guard, the Japanese side will send Ii to monitor. The Jixian incident will not be expanded. I will send personnel to investigate to facilitate an early resolution. The puppet police stationed at Gubeikou Nantianmen have decided to withdraw 20 li and will be withdrawn within a week. The reception of Ma Lan Yu is only a matter of time. The Japanese side has decided to return it to China and is ready to carry out the handover as soon as possible. It is expected that all issues in the war zone will be completely resolved within a month. The issue of traffic was not mentioned at the Yuguan meeting. Whether it was mentioned at the Beidaihe meeting is unknown because I did not participate. (17th)

Remnants of the Ye Bandit Disturbed Junmen and Retreated in Defeat; Xiao Bandit of Yudu Attacked Ganxian Unsuccessfully

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since retreating to Huichang, the communist bandits have changed their strategy and plan to extend to eastern and western Jiangxi. In eastern Jiangxi, one force is confronting the bandit suppression army in eastern Fujian Province. In addition to using Xiao Ke's force to contain the Hunan Army in western Jiangxi, they recently planned to use a main force to break out of Ganzhou from Yudu, Xingguo, and other places to open up the road to western Jiangxi. Therefore, there have been communist bandit activities near Ganxian in recent days. The Second and Fourth Divisions of the First Column have recently discovered the presence of communist bandits in the Benmao Dian area. At dawn on the 7th, about 700 members of the pseudo-Red Guard, with 400 guns, fled from Yudu to Xiaoben, which belongs to Ganxian County. Song Shitai's regiment, stationed in Hanfang by the Second Division of the defense army, rushed to suppress them. At 1:00 PM that afternoon, Song's regiment fought the bandits fiercely for two hours. The bandits were defeated and retreated towards Mailing. More than 100 communist bandits were wounded and killed, and one artillery piece, two machine guns, and two red flags were captured. The next day, other communist bandit teams were discovered in Maodian. The Fourth Division of the defense army, upon receiving the report, sent the teaching regiment of the division, led by Zeng Zhaoji, to suppress them. On the evening of the 8th, they crossed the river from Hualinsi, and on the 9th, they approached Maodian and besieged the communist pseudo-independent battalion in Wanshou Palace Shangxia Gate Market. At the same time, the 11th regiment, led by Li Guoliang, was sent from the east bank of the Gan River to Maodian to respond. Zeng's regiment received reinforcements and soon entered Maodian, and burned the bandit stronghold on Yunzishan. The remaining bandits fled towards Huanglongpu. (13th)
